Lex is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\\n359: // It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\\n360: // Comments are skipped.\\n361: //\\n362: // The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\\n363: // the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\\n364: // and error handling.\\n365: //\\n366: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\\n367: func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\\n368: \\tvar typ ItemType\\n369: \\n370: \\tif p.injecting {\\n371: \\t\\tp.injecting = false\\n372: \\t\\treturn int(p.inject)\\n373: \\t}\\n374: \\t// Skip comments.\\n375: \\tfor {\\n376: \\t\\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\\n377: \\t\\ttyp posrange.PositionRange{\\n386: \\t\\t\\tStart: p.lex.start,\\n387: \\t\\t\\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\\n388: \\t\\t}\\n389: \\t\\tp.addParseErr(pos, triggered\\n406: // by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\\n407: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\\n408: func (*parser) Error(string) {\\n409: }\\n410: \\n411: // InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\\n412: // consumed by the generated parser.\\n413: // This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\\n414: // https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\\n415: // Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this \\tp.injecting = true\\n429: }\\n430: \\n431: func (p *parser) newBinaryExpression(lhs Node, op Item, modifiers, rhs Node) *BinaryExpr {\\n432: \\tret := modifiers.(*BinaryExpr)\\n433: \\n434: Lex is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\\n359: // It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\\n360: // Comments are skipped.\\n361: //\\n362: // The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\\n363: // the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\\n364: // and error handling.\\n365: //\\n366: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\\n367: func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\\n368: \\tvar typ ItemType\\n369: \\n370: \\tif p.injecting {\\n371: \\t\\tp.injecting = false\\n372: \\t\\treturn int(p.inject)\\n373: \\t}\\n374: \\t// Skip comments.\\n375: \\tfor {\\n376: \\t\\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\\n377: \\t\\ttyp {\\n409: }\\n410: \\n411: // InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\\n412: // consumed by the generated parser.\\n413: // This allows having multiple start \\t}\\n707: \\treturn f\\n708: }\\n709: \\n710: // expectType checks the type of the node and raises an error if it\\n711: // is not of the expected type.\\n712: func (p *parser) expectType(node Node, Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\n360: // Comments are skipped.\n361: //\n362: // The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\n363: // the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\n364: // and error handling.\n365: //\n366: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n367: func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\n368: \tvar typ ItemType\n369: \n370: \tif p.injecting {\n371: \t\tp.injecting = false\n372: \t\treturn int(p.inject)\n373: \t}\n374: \t// Skip comments.\n375: \tfor {\n376: \t\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\n377: \t\ttyp = lval.item.Typ\n378: \t\tif typ != COMMENT {\n379: \t\t\tbreak\n380: \t\t}\n381: \t}\n382: \n383: \tswitch typ {\n384: \tcase ERROR:\n385: \t\tpos := posrange.PositionRange{\n386: \t\t\tStart: p.lex.start,\n387: \t\t\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\n388: \t\t}\n389: \t\tp.addParseErr(pos, errors.New(p.yyParser.lval.item.Val))\n390: \n391: \t\t// Tells yacc that this is the end of input.\n392: \t\treturn 0\n393: \tcase EOF:\n394: \t\tlval.item.Typ = \treturn int(typ)\n401: }\n402: \n403: // Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n404: //\n405: // It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\n406: // by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\n407: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n408: func (*parser) Error(string) {\n409: }\n410: \n411: // InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\n412: // consumed by the generated parser.\n413: // This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\n414: // https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\n415: // Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\n416: // Trying to provided AST. This includes type checking.\n720: func (p *parser) checkAST(node Node) (typ ValueType) {\n721: \t// For expressions the type is determined by their Type function.\n722: \t// Lists do not have a type but are not invalid either.\n723: \tswitch n := node.(type) {\n724: \tcase Expressions:\n725: \t\ttyp = ValueTypeNone\n726: \tcase Expr:\n727: \t\ttyp = n.Type()\n728: \tdefault:\n729: typing.\n734: \tswitch n := node.(type) {\n735: \tcase *EvalStmt:\n736: \t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n737: \t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n738: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Expr.PositionRange(), \"evaluation ValueTypeScalar && n.LHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar {\n780: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"comparisons between scalars must use BOOL modifier\")\n781: \t\t}\n782: \n783: \t\tif n.Op.IsSetOperator() && n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToOne {\n784: \t\t\tn.VectorMatching.Card = CardManyToMany\n785: \t\t}\n786: \n787: \t\tfor _, l1 := range n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels {\n788: \t\t\tfor _, l2 := \t\t\t\t}\n792: \t\t\t}\n793: \t\t}\n794: \n795: \t\tif !n.Op.IsOperator() {\n796: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"binary expression does not support operator %q\", n.Op)\n797: \t\t}\n798: \t\tif rt != ValueTypeScalar && rt != ValueTypeVector {\n802: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.RHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n803: \t\t}\n804: \tp.yyParser.Parse(p)\n956: \n957: \treturn p.generatedParserResult\n958: }\n959: \n960: func (p *parser) newLabelMatcher(label, operator, value Item) *labels.Matcher {\n961: \top := visiting a Node and its child nodes. The Visit method is\\n337: // invoked for each node with the path leading to the node provided additionally.\\n338: // If the result visitor w is not nil and no error, Walk visits each of the children\\n339: // of node with the visitor w, followed by a call of w.Visit(nil, nil).\\n340: type Visitor interface {\\n341: \\tVisit(node Node, path []Node) (w Visitor, err error)\\n342: }\\n343: \\n344: // Walk traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\\n345: // v.Visit(node, path); node must not be nil. If the visitor w returned by\\n346: // v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\\n347: // invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\\n348: // followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\\n349: // As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\\n350: func Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\\n351: \\tvar err error\\n352: \\tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\\n353: \\t\\treturn err\\n354: \\t}\\n355: \\tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\\n356: \\n357: \\tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\\n358: \\t\\tif pathToHere == nil {\\n359: \\t\\t\\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\\n360: \\t\\t}\\n361: \\t\\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\\n362: \\t\\t\\treturn err\\n363: \\t\\t}\\n364: \\t}\\n365: \\n366: \\t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\\n367: \\treturn err\\n368: }\\n369: \\n370: func ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\\n371: \\tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\\n372: \\tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\\n373: \\t\\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\\n374: \\t\\tif ok {\\n375: \\t\\t\\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\\n376: \\t\\t}\\n377: \\t\\treturn nil\\n378: \\t})\\n379: \\treturn selectors\\n380: }\\n381: \\n382: type inspector func(Node, []Node) error\\n383: \\n384: func (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\\n385: \\tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\\n386: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n387: \\t}\\n388: \\n389: \\treturn f, nil\\n390: }\\n391: \\n392: // Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\\n393: // f(node, path); node must not be nil. If f returns a nil error, Inspect invokes f\\n394: // for all the non-nil children of node, recursively.\\n395: // Note: path may be overwritten after f returns; copy path if you need to retain it.\\n396: func Inspect(node Node, f inspector) {\\n397: \\tvar pathBuf [4]Node        // To reduce allocations during recursion.\\n398: \\tWalk(f, node, pathBuf[:0]) //nolint:errcheck\\n399: }\\n400: \\n401: // ChildrenIter returns an iterator over all child nodes of a syntax tree node.\\n402: func ChildrenIter(node Node) func(func(Node) bool) {\\n403: \\treturn func(yield func(Node) bool) {\\n404: \\t\\t// According to lore, these switches have significantly better performance than interfaces\\n405: \\t\\tswitch n := node.(type) {\\n406: \\t\\tcase *EvalStmt:\\n407: The Visit method is\\n337: // invoked for each node with the path leading to the node provided additionally.\\n338: // If the result visitor w is not nil and no error, Walk visits each of the children\\n339: // of node with the visitor w, followed by a call of w.Visit(nil, nil).\\n340: type Visitor interface {\\n341: \\tVisit(node Node, path []Node) (w Visitor, err error)\\n342: }\\n343: \\n344: // Walk traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\\n345: // v.Visit(node, path); node must not be nil. If the visitor w returned by\\n346: // v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\\n347: // invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\\n348: // followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\\n349: // As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\\n350: func Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\\n351: \\tvar err error\\n352: \\tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\\n353: \\t\\treturn err\\n354: \\t}\\n355: \\tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\\n356: \\n357: \\tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\\n358: \\t\\tif pathToHere == nil {\\n359: \\t\\t\\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\\n360: \\t\\t}\\n361: \\t\\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\\n362: \\t\\t\\treturn err\\n363: \\t\\t}\\n364: \\t}\\n365: \\n366: \\t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\\n367: \\treturn err\\n368: }\\n369: \\n370: func ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\\n371: \\tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\\n372: \\tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\\n373: \\t\\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\\n374: \\t\\tif ok {\\n375: \\t\\t\\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\\n376: \\t\\t}\\n377: \\t\\treturn nil\\n378: \\t})\\n379: \\treturn selectors\\n380: }\\n381: \\n382: type inspector func(Node, []Node) error\\n383: \\n384: func (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\\n385: \\tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\\n386: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n387: \\t}\\n388: \\n389: \\treturn f, nil\\n390: }\\n391: \\n392: // Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\\n393: // f(node, path); node must not be nil. If f returns a nil error, Inspect invokes f\\n394: // for all the non-nil children of node, recursively.\\n395: // Note: path may be overwritten after f returns; copy path if you need to retain it.\\n396: func Inspect(node Node, f inspector) {\\n397: \\tvar pathBuf [4]Node        // To reduce allocations during recursion.\\n398: \\tWalk(f, node, pathBuf[:0]) //nolint:errcheck\\n399: }\\n400: \\n401: // ChildrenIter returns an iterator over all child nodes of a syntax tree node.\\n402: func ChildrenIter(node Node) func(func(Node) bool) {\\n403: \\treturn func(yield func(Node) bool) {\\n404: \\t\\t// According to lore, these switches have significantly better performance than interfaces\\n405: \\t\\tswitch n := node.(type) {\\n406: \\t\\tcase *EvalStmt:\\n407: \\t\\t\\tyield(n.Expr)\\n408: \\t\\tcase Expressions:\\n409: \\t\\t\\tfor _, e := range n {\\n410: \\t\\t\\t\\tif !yield(e) {\\n411: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n412: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n413: \\t\\t\\t}\\n414: \\t\\tcase *AggregateExpr:\\n415: \\t\\t\\tif n.Expr != nil {\\n416: \\t\\t\\t\\tif !yield(n.Expr) {\\n417: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n418: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n419: \\t\\t\\t}\\n420: \\t\\t\\tif n.Param != nil {\\n421: \\t\\t\\t\\tyield(n.Param)\\n422: \\t\\t\\t}\\n423: \\t\\tcase *BinaryExpr:\\n424: \\t\\t\\tif !yield(n.LHS) {\\n425: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n426: \\t\\t\\t}\\n427: \\t\\t\\tyield(n.RHS)\\n428: \\t\\tcase *Call:\\n429: \\t\\t\\tfor _, e := range n.Args {\\n430: \\t\\t\\t\\tif !yield(e) {\\n431: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n432: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n433: \\t\\t\\t}\\n434: *MatrixSelector:\\n441: \\t\\t\\tyield(n.VectorSelector)\\n442: \\t\\tcase *StepInvariantExpr:\\n443: \\t\\t\\tyield(n.Expr)\\n444: \\t\\tcase *NumberLiteral, *StringLiteral, *VectorSelector:\\n445: []Node{}\\n456: \\tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\\n457: \\t\\tret = append(ret, e)\\n458: \\t}\\n459: \\treturn ret\\n460: }\\n461: \\n462: // mergeRanges is a helper function to merge the Visitor allows visiting a Node and its child nodes. The Visit method is\n337: // invoked for each node with the path leading to the node provided additionally.\n338: // If the result visitor w is not nil and no error, Walk visits each of the children\n339: // of node with the visitor w, followed by a call of w.Visit(nil, nil).\n340: type Visitor interface {\n341: \tVisit(node Node, path []Node) (w Visitor, err error)\n342: }\n343: \n344: // Walk traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n345: // v.Visit(node, path); node must not be nil. If the visitor w returned by\n346: // v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\n347: // invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\n348: // followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\n349: // As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\n350: func Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\n351: \tvar err error\n352: \tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\n353: \t\treturn err\n354: \t}\n355: \tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\n356: \n357: \tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\n358: \t\tif pathToHere == nil {\n359: \t\t\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\n360: \t\t}\n361: \t\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\n362: \t\t\treturn err\n363: \t\t}\n364: \t}\n365: \n366: \t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\n367: \treturn err\n368: }\n369: \n370: func ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\n371: \tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\n372: \tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\n373: \t\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\n374: \t\tif ok {\n375: \t\t\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\n376: \t\t}\n377: \t\treturn nil\n378: \t})\n379: \treturn selectors\n380: }\n381: \n382: type inspector func(Node, []Node) error\n383: \n384: func (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\n385: \tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\n386: \t\treturn nil, err\n387: \t}\n388: \n389: \treturn f, nil\n390: }\n391: \n392: // Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n393: // f(node, path); node must not be nil. If f returns a nil error, Inspect invokes f\n394: // for all the non-nil children of node, recursively.\n395: // Note: path may be overwritten after f returns; copy path if you need to retain it.\n396: func Inspect(node Node, f inspector) {\n397: \tvar pathBuf [4]Node        // To reduce allocations during recursion.\n398: \tWalk(f, node, pathBuf[:0]) //nolint:errcheck\n399: }\n400: \n401: // ChildrenIter returns an iterator over all child nodes of a syntax tree node.\n402: func ChildrenIter(node Node) func(func(Node) bool) {\n403: \treturn func(yield func(Node) bool) {\n404: \t\t// According to lore, these switches have significantly better performance than interfaces\n405: \t\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n406: \t\tcase *EvalStmt:\n407: \t\t\tyield(n.Expr)\n408: \t\tcase \\t}\\n388: \\treturn l\\n389: }\\n390: \\n391: // lineComment is the character that starts a line comment.\\n392: const lineComment = \\\"#\\\"\\n393: \\n394: // lexStatements is the top-level state for lexing.\\n395: func lexStatements(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n396: \\tif l.histogramState != histogramStateNone {\\n397: \\t\\treturn lexHistogram\\n398: \\t}\\n399: \\tif l.braceOpen {\\n400: The initial escaping character (\\\\)\\n767: // has already been seen.\\n768: //\\n769: // NOTE: This function as well as the helper function digitVal() and associated\\n770: // tests have been adapted from the corresponding functions in the \\\"go/scanner\\\"\\n771: // package of the Go standard library to work for Prometheus-style strings.\\n772: // None of the actual escaping/quoting logic was changed in this function - it\\n773: // was only modified to integrate with our lexer.\\n774: func lexEscape(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n775: \\tvar n int\\n776: \\tvar base, maxVal uint32\\n777: \\n778: \\tch := l.next()\\n779: \\tswitch ch {\\n780: \\tcase 'a', 'b', 'f', 'n', 'r', 't', 'v', '\\\\\\\\', l.stringOpen:\\n781: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n782: \\tcase '0', '1', '2', '3', '4', '5', '6', '7':\\n783: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 3, 8, 255\\n784: \\tcase 'x':\\n785: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n786: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 2, 16, 255\\n787: \\tcase 'u':\\n788: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n789: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 4, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n790: \\tcase 'U':\\n791: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n792: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 8, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n793: \\tcase eof:\\n794: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n795: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n796: \\tdefault:\\n797: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unknown escape sequence %#U\\\", ch)\\n798: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n799: \\t}\\n800: \\n801: \\tvar x uint32\\n802: \\tfor n > 0 {\\n803: \\t\\td := uint32(digitVal(ch))\\n804: \\t\\tif d >= base {\\n805: \\t\\t\\tif ch == eof {\\n806: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n807: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n808: \\t\\t\\t}\\n809: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"illegal character %#U in escape sequence\\\", ch)\\n810: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n811: \\t\\t}\\n812: \\t\\tx = x*base + d\\n813: \\t\\tn--\\n814: \\n815: \\t\\t// Don't seek after last rune.\\n816: \\t\\tif n > 0 {\\n817: \\t\\t\\tch = l.next()\\n818: \\t\\t}\\n819: \\t}\\n820: \\n821: \\tif x > maxVal || 0xD800 <= x && x < 0xE000 {\\n822: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence is an invalid Unicode code point\\\")\\n823: \\t}\\n824: \\treturn lexString\\n825: }\\n826: \\n827: // digitVal returns the digit value of a rune or 16 in case the rune does not\\n828: // represent a valid digit.\\n829: func digitVal(ch rune) int {\\n830: \\tswitch {\\n831: \\tcase '0' <= ch && ch <= '9':\\n832: \\t\\treturn int(ch - '0')\\n833: \\tcase 'a' <= ch && ch <= 'f':\\n834: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'a' + 10)\\n835: \\tcase 'A' <= ch && ch <= 'F':\\n836: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'A' + 10)\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\treturn 16 // Larger than any legal digit val.\\n839: }\\n840: \\n841: // skipSpaces skips the spaces until a non-space is encountered.\\n842: func skipSpaces(l *Lexer) {\\n843: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n844: \\t\\tl.next()\\n845: \\t}\\n846: \\tl.ignore()\\n847: }\\n848: \\n849: // lexString scans a quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n850: func lexString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n851: Loop:\\n852: \\tfor {\\n853: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n854: \\t\\tcase '\\\\\\\\':\\n855: \\t\\t\\treturn lexEscape\\n856: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n857: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n858: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n859: \\t\\tcase eof, '\\\\n':\\n860: \\t\\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"unterminated quoted string\\\")\\n861: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n862: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n863: \\t\\t}\\n864: \\t}\\n865: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n866: \\treturn lexStatements\\n867: }\\n868: \\n869: // lexRawString scans a raw quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n870: func lexRawString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n871: Loop:\\n872: \\tfor {\\n873: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n874: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n875: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n876: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n877: \\t\\tcase eof:\\n878: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unterminated raw string\\\")\\n879: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n880: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n881: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n882: \\t\\t}\\n883: \\t}\\n884: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n885: \\treturn lexStatements\\n886: }\\n887: \\n888: // lexSpace scans a run of space characters. One space has already been seen.\\n889: func lexSpace(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n890: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n891: \\t\\tl.next()\\n892: \\t}\\n893: \\tl.ignore()\\n894: \\treturn lexStatements\\n895: }\\n896: \\n897: // lexLineComment scans a line comment. }\\n356: \\n357: // errorf returns an error token and terminates the scan by passing\\n358: // back a nil pointer that will be the next state, terminating l.NextItem.\\n359: func (l *Lexer) The initial escaping character (\\\\)\\n767: // has already been seen.\\n768: //\\n769: // NOTE: This function as well as the helper function digitVal() and associated\\n770: // tests have been adapted from the corresponding functions in the \\\"go/scanner\\\"\\n771: // package of the Go standard library to work for Prometheus-style strings.\\n772: // None of the actual escaping/quoting logic was changed in this function - it\\n773: // was only modified to integrate with our lexer.\\n774: func lexEscape(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n775: \\tvar n int\\n776: \\tvar base, maxVal uint32\\n777: \\n778: \\tch := l.next()\\n779: \\tswitch ch {\\n780: \\tcase 'a', 'b', 'f', 'n', 'r', 't', 'v', '\\\\\\\\', l.stringOpen:\\n781: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n782: \\tcase '0', '1', '2', '3', '4', '5', '6', '7':\\n783: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 3, 8, 255\\n784: \\tcase 'x':\\n785: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n786: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 2, 16, 255\\n787: \\tcase 'u':\\n788: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n789: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 4, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n790: \\tcase 'U':\\n791: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n792: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 8, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n793: \\tcase eof:\\n794: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n795: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n796: \\tdefault:\\n797: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unknown escape sequence %#U\\\", ch)\\n798: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n799: \\t}\\n800: \\n801: \\tvar x uint32\\n802: \\tfor n > 0 {\\n803: \\t\\td := uint32(digitVal(ch))\\n804: \\t\\tif d >= base {\\n805: \\t\\t\\tif ch == eof {\\n806: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n807: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n808: \\t\\t\\t}\\n809: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"illegal character %#U in escape sequence\\\", ch)\\n810: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n811: \\t\\t}\\n812: \\t\\tx = x*base + d\\n813: \\t\\tn--\\n814: \\n815: \\t\\t// Don't seek after last rune.\\n816: \\t\\tif n > 0 {\\n817: \\t\\t\\tch = l.next()\\n818: \\t\\t}\\n819: \\t}\\n820: \\n821: \\tif x > maxVal || 0xD800 <= x && x < 0xE000 {\\n822: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence is an invalid Unicode code point\\\")\\n823: \\t}\\n824: \\treturn lexString\\n825: }\\n826: \\n827: // digitVal returns the digit value of a rune or 16 in case the rune does not\\n828: // represent a valid digit.\\n829: func digitVal(ch rune) int {\\n830: \\tswitch {\\n831: \\tcase '0' <= ch && ch <= '9':\\n832: \\t\\treturn int(ch - '0')\\n833: \\tcase 'a' <= ch && ch <= 'f':\\n834: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'a' + 10)\\n835: \\tcase 'A' <= ch && ch <= 'F':\\n836: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'A' + 10)\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\treturn 16 // Larger than any legal digit val.\\n839: }\\n840: \\n841: // skipSpaces skips the spaces until a non-space is encountered.\\n842: func skipSpaces(l *Lexer) {\\n843: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n844: \\t\\tl.next()\\n845: \\t}\\n846: \\tl.ignore()\\n847: }\\n848: \\n849: // lexString scans a quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n850: func lexString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n851: Loop:\\n852: \\tfor {\\n853: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n854: \\t\\tcase '\\\\\\\\':\\n855: \\t\\t\\treturn lexEscape\\n856: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n857: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n858: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n859: \\t\\tcase eof, '\\\\n':\\n860: \\t\\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"unterminated quoted string\\\")\\n861: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n862: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n863: \\t\\t}\\n864: \\t}\\n865: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n866: \\treturn lexStatements\\n867: }\\n868: \\n869: // lexRawString scans a raw quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n870: func lexRawString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n871: Loop:\\n872: \\tfor {\\n873: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n874: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n875: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n876: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n877: \\t\\tcase eof:\\n878: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unterminated raw string\\\")\\n879: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n880: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n881: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n882: \\t\\t}\\n883: \\t}\\n884: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n885: \\treturn lexStatements\\n886: }\\n887: \\n888: // lexSpace scans a run of space characters. One space has already been seen.\\n889: func lexSpace(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n890: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n891: \\t\\tl.next()\\n892: \\t}\\n893: \\tl.ignore()\\n894: \\treturn lexStatements\\n895: }\\n896: \\n897: // lexLineComment scans a line comment. \t\tl.emit(ADD)\n546: \t\treturn lexValueSequence\n547: \tcase histogramStateSub:\n548: \t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateNone\n549: \t\tl.next()\n550: \t\tl.emit(SUB)\n551: \t\treturn lexSpace\n561: \tcase isAlpha(r):\n562: \t\tl.backup()\n563: \t\treturn lexHistogramDescriptor\n564: \tcase r == ':':\n565: \t\tl.emit(COLON)\n566: \t\treturn lexHistogram\n567: \tcase r == '-':\n568: \t\tl.emit(SUB)\n569: \t\treturn lexHistogram\n570: \tcase r == 'x':\n571: \t\tl.emit(TIMES)\n572: \t\treturn lexNumber\n573: \tcase isDigit(r):\n574: \t\tl.backup()\n575: \t\treturn lexNumber\n576: \tcase r == '[':\n577: \t\tl.bracketOpen = true\n578: \t\tl.gotColon = false\n579: \t\tl.gotDuration = false\n580: \t\tl.emit(LEFT_BRACKET)\n581: \t\treturn lexBuckets\n582: \tcase r == '}' && l.peek() == '}':\n583: \t\tl.next()\n584: \t\tl.emit(CLOSE_HIST)\n585: \t\tswitch l.peek() {\n586: \t\tcase 'x':\n587: \t\t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateMul\n588: \t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n589: \t\tcase '+':\n590: \t\t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateAdd\n591: \t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n592: \t\tcase '-':\n593: \t\t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateSub\n594: \t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n595: \t\tdefault:\n596: \t\t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateNone\n597: \t\t\treturn lexValueSequence\n598: \t\t}\n599: \tdefault:\n600: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"histogram description incomplete unexpected: %q\", r)\n601: \t}\n602: }\n603: \n604: func lexHistogramDescriptor(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n605: Loop:\n606: \tfor {\n607: \t\tswitch r := l.next(); {\n608: \t\tcase isAlpha(r):\n609: \t\t\t// absorb.\n610: \t\tdefault:\n611: \t\t\tl.backup()\n612: \n613: \t\t\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\n614: \t\t\tif desc, ok := histogramDesc[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\n615: \t\t\t\tif l.peek() == ':' {\n616: \t\t\t\t\tl.emit(desc)\n617: \t\t\t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n618: \t\t\t\t}\n619: \t\t\t\tl.errorf(\"missing `:` for histogram descriptor\")\n620: \t\t\t\tbreak Loop\n621: \t\t\t}\n622: \t\t\t// Current word is Inf or NaN.\n623: \t\t\tif desc, ok := key[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\n624: \t\t\t\tif desc == NUMBER {\n625: \t\t\t\t\tl.emit(desc)\n626: \t\t\t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n627: \t\t\t\t}\n628: \t\t\t}\n629: \t\t\tif desc, ok := counterResetHints[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\n630: \t\t\t\tl.emit(desc)\n631: \t\t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n632: \t\t\t}\n633: \n634: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"bad histogram descriptor found: %q\", word)\n635: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n636: \t\t}\n637: \t}\n638: \treturn lexStatements\n639: }\n640: \n641: func lexBuckets(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n642: \tswitch r := l.next(); {\n643: \tcase isSpace(r):\n644: \t\tl.emit(SPACE)\n645: \t\treturn lexSpace\n646: \tcase r == '-':\n647: \t\tl.emit(SUB)\n648: \t\treturn lexNumber\n649: \tcase isDigit(r):\n650: \t\tl.backup()\n651: \t\treturn lexNumber\n652: \tcase r == ']':\n653: \t\tl.bracketOpen = false\n654: \t\tl.emit(RIGHT_BRACKET)\n655: \t\treturn lexHistogram\n656: \tcase isAlpha(r):\n657: \t\t// Current word is Inf or NaN.\n658: \t\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\n659: \t\tif desc, ok := key[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\n660: \t\t\tif desc == NUMBER {\n661: \t\t\t\tl.emit(desc)\n662: \t\t\t\treturn lexStatements\n663: \t\t\t}\n664: \t\t}\n665: \t\treturn lexBuckets\n666: \tdefault:\n667: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"invalid character in buckets description: %q\", r)\n668: \t}\n669: }\n670: \n671: // lexInsideBraces scans the inside of a vector selector. Keywords are ignored and\n672: // scanned as identifiers.\n673: func lexInsideBraces(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n674: \tif strings.HasPrefix(l.input[l.pos:], lineComment) {\n675: \t\treturn lexLineComment\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tswitch r := l.next(); {\n679: \tcase r == eof:\n680: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"unexpected end of input inside braces\")\n681: \tcase isSpace(r):\n682: \t\treturn lexSpace\n683: \tcase isAlpha(r):\n684: \t\tl.backup()\n685: \t\treturn lexIdentifier\n686: \tcase r == ',':\n687: \t\tl.emit(COMMA)\n688: \tcase r == '\"' || r == '\\'':\n689: \t\tl.stringOpen = r\n690: \t\treturn lexString\n691: \tcase r == '`':\n692: \t\tl.stringOpen = r\n693: \t\treturn lexRawString\n694: \tcase r == '=':\n695: \t\tif l.next() == '~' {\n696: \t\t\tl.emit(EQL_REGEX)\n697: \t\t\tbreak\n698: \t\t}\n699: \t\tl.backup()\n700: \t\tl.emit(EQL)\n701: \tcase r == '!':\n702: \t\tswitch nr := l.next(); {\n732: \tcase r == eof:\n733: \t\treturn lexStatements\n734: \tcase r == '{' && l.peek() == '{':\n735: \t\tif l.histogramState != histogramStateNone {\n736: \t\t\treturn l.errorf(\"unexpected histogram opening {{\")\n737: \t\t}\n738: \t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateOpen\n739: \t\tl.next()\n740: \t\tl.emit(OPEN_HIST)\n741: \t\treturn lexHistogram\n742: \tcase isSpace(r):\n743: \t\tl.emit(SPACE)\n744: \t\tlexSpace(l)\n745: \tcase r == '+':\n746: \t\tl.emit(ADD)\n747: \tcase r == '-':\n748: \t\tl.emit(SUB)\n749: \tcase r == 'x':\n750: \t\tl.emit(TIMES)\n751: \tcase r == '_':\n752: \t\tl.emit(BLANK)\n753: \tcase isDigit(r) || (r == '.' && isDigit(l.peek())):\n754: \t\tl.backup()\n755: \t\tlexNumber(l)\n756: \tcase isAlpha(r):\n757: \t\tl.backup()\n758: \t\t// We might lex invalid Items here but this will be caught by the parser.\n759: \t\treturn lexKeywordOrIdentifier\n760: \tdefault:\n761: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"unexpected character in series sequence: %q\", r)\n762: \t}\n763: \treturn lexValueSequence\n764: }\n765: \n766: // lexEscape scans a string escape sequence. The initial escaping character (\\)\n767: // has already been seen.\n768: //\n769: // NOTE: This function as well as the helper function digitVal() and associated\n770: // tests have been adapted from the corresponding functions in the \"go/scanner\"\n771: // package of the Go standard library to work for Prometheus-style strings.\n772: // None of the actual escaping/quoting logic was changed in this function - it\n773: // was only modified to integrate with our lexer.\n774: func lexEscape(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n775: \tvar n int\n776: \tvar base, maxVal uint32\n777: \n778: \tch := l.next()\n779: \tswitch ch {\n780: \tcase 'a', 'b', 'f', 'n', 'r', 't', 'v', '\\\\', l.stringOpen:\n781: \t\treturn lexString\n782: \tcase '0', '1', '2', '3', '4', '5', '6', '7':\n783: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 3, 8, 255\n784: \tcase 'x':\n785: \t\tch = l.next()\n786: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 2, 16, 255\n787: \tcase 'u':\n788: \t\tch = l.next()\n789: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 4, 16, unicode.MaxRune\n790: \tcase 'U':\n791: \t\tch = l.next()\n792: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 8, 16, unicode.MaxRune\n793: \tcase eof:\n794: \t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence not terminated\")\n795: \t\treturn lexString\n796: \tdefault:\n797: \t\tl.errorf(\"unknown escape sequence %#U\", ch)\n798: \t\treturn lexString\n799: \t}\n800: \n801: \tvar x uint32\n802: \tfor n > 0 {\n803: \t\td := uint32(digitVal(ch))\n804: \t\tif d >= base {\n805: \t\t\tif ch == eof {\n806: \t\t\t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence not terminated\")\n807: \t\t\t\treturn lexString\n808: \t\t\t}\n809: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"illegal character %#U in escape sequence\", ch)\n810: \t\t\treturn lexString\n811: \t\t}\n812: \t\tx = x*base + d\n813: \t\tn--\n814: \n815: \t\t// Don't seek after last rune.\n816: \t\tif n > 0 {\n817: \t\t\tch = l.next()\n818: \t\t}\n819: \t}\n820: \n821: \tif x > maxVal || 0xD800 <= x && x < 0xE000 {\n822: \t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence is an invalid Unicode code point\")\n823: \t}\n824: \treturn lexString\n825: }\n826: \n827: // digitVal returns the digit value of a rune or 16 in case the rune does not\n828: // represent a valid digit.\n829: func digitVal(ch rune) int {\n830: \tswitch {\n831: \tcase '0' <= ch && ch <= '9':\n832: \t\treturn int(ch - '0')\n833: \tcase 'a' <= ch && ch <= 'f':\n834: \t\treturn int(ch - 'a' + 10)\n835: \tcase 'A' <= ch && ch <= 'F':\n836: \t\treturn int(ch - 'A' + 10)\n837: \t}\n838: \treturn 16 // Larger than any legal digit val.\n839: }\n840: \n841: // skipSpaces skips the spaces until a non-space is encountered.\n842: func skipSpaces(l *Lexer) {\n843: \tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\n844: \t\tl.next()\n845: \t}\n846: \tl.ignore()\n847: }\n848: \n849: // lexString scans a quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\n850: func lexString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n851: Loop:\n852: \tfor {\n853: \t\tswitch l.next() {\n854: \t\tcase '\\\\':\n855: \t\t\treturn lexEscape\n856: \t\tcase utf8.RuneError:\n857: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"invalid UTF-8 rune\")\n858: \t\t\treturn lexString\n859: \t\tcase eof, '\\n':\n860: \t\t\treturn l.errorf(\"unterminated quoted string\")\n861: \t\tcase l.stringOpen:\n862: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n863: \t\t}\n864: \t}\n865: \tl.emit(STRING)\n866: \treturn lexStatements\n867: }\n868: \n869: // lexRawString scans a raw quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\n870: func lexRawString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n871: Loop:\n872: \tfor {\n873: \t\tswitch l.next() {\n874: \t\tcase utf8.RuneError:\n875: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"invalid UTF-8 rune\")\n876: \t\t\treturn lexRawString\n877: \t\tcase eof:\n878: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"unterminated raw string\")\n879: \t\t\treturn lexRawString\n880: \t\tcase l.stringOpen:\n881: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n882: \t\t}\n883: \t}\n884: \tl.emit(STRING)\n885: \treturn lexStatements\n886: }\n887: \n888: // lexSpace scans a run of space characters. One space has already been seen.\n889: func lexSpace(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n890: \tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\n891: \t\tl.next()\n892: \t}\n893: \tl.ignore()\n894: \treturn lexStatements\n895: }\n896: \n897: // lexLineComment scans a line comment. Left comment marker is known to be present.\n898: func lexLineComment(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n899: \tl.pos += posrange.Pos(len(lineComment))\n900: \tfor r := l.next(); !isEndOfLine(r) && r != eof; {\n901: \t\tr = l.next()\n902: \t}\n903: \tl.backup()\n904: \tl.emit(COMMENT)\n905: \treturn lexStatements\n906: }\n907: \n908: // lexNumber scans a number: decimal, hex, oct or float.\n909: func lexNumber(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n910: \tif !l.scanNumber() {\n911: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"bad number syntax: %q\", l.input[l.start:l.pos])\n912: \t}\n913: \tl.emit(NUMBER)\n914: \treturn lexStatements\n915: }\n916: \n917: func (l *Lexer) scanDurationKeyword() bool {\n918: \tfor {\n919: \t\tswitch r := l.next(); {\n920: \t\tcase isAlpha(r):\n921: \t\t\t// absorb.\n922: \t\tdefault:\n923: \t\t\tl.backup()\n924: \t\t\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\n925: \t\t\tkw := strings.ToLower(word)\n926: \t\t\tswitch kw {\n927: \t\t\tcase \"step\":\n928: \t\t\t\tl.emit(STEP)\n929: \t\t\t\treturn true\n930: \t\t\tcase \"range\":\n931: \t\t\t\tl.emit(RANGE)\n932: \t\t\t\treturn true\n933: \t\t\tcase \"min\":\n934: \t\t\t\tl.emit(MIN)\n935: \t\t\t\treturn true\n936: \t\t\tcase \"max\":\n937: \t\t\t\tl.emit(MAX)\n938: \t\t\t\treturn true\n939: \t\t\tdefault:\n940: \t\t\t\treturn false\n941: \t\t\t}\n942: \t\t}\n943: \t}\n944: }\n945: \n946: // lexNumberOrDuration scans a number or a duration Item.\n947: func lexNumberOrDuration(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n948: \tif l.scanNumber() {\n949: \t\tl.emit(NUMBER)\n950: \t\treturn lexStatements\n951: \t}\n952: \t// Next two chars must be a valid unit and a non-alphanumeric.\n953: \tif acceptRemainingDuration(l) {\n954: \t\tl.backup()\n955: \t\tl.emit(DURATION)\n956: \t\treturn lexStatements\n957: \t}\n958: \treturn l.errorf(\"bad number or duration syntax: %q\", l.input[l.start:l.pos])\n959: }\n960: \n961: func acceptRemainingDuration(l *Lexer) bool {\n962: \t// Next two char must be a valid duration.\n963: \tif !l.accept(\"smhdwy\") {\n964: \t\treturn false\n965: \t}\n966: \t// Support for ms. Bad units like hs, ys will be caught when we actually\n967: \t// parse the duration.\n968: \tl.accept(\"s\")\n969: \t// Next char can be another number then a unit.\n970: \tfor l.accept(\"0123456789\") {\n971: \t\tfor l.accept(\"0123456789\") {\n972: \t\t}\n973: \t\t// y is no longer in the list as it should always come first in\n974: \t\t// durations.\n975: \t\tif !l.accept(\"smhdw\") {\n976: \t\t\treturn false\n977: \t\t}\n978: \t\t// Support for ms. Bad units like hs, ys will be caught when we actually\n979: \t\t// parse the duration.\n980: \t\tl.accept(\"s\")\n981: \t}\n982: \treturn !isAlphaNumeric(l.next())\n983: }\n984: \n985: // scanNumber scans numbers of different formats. The scanned Item is\n986: // not necessarily a valid number. This case is caught by the parser.\n987: func (l *Lexer) scanNumber() bool {\n988: \tinitialPos := l.pos\n989: \t// Modify the digit pattern if the number is hexadecimal.\n990: \tdigitPattern := \"0123456789\"\n991: \t// Disallow hexadecimal in series descriptions as the syntax is ambiguous.\n992: \tif !l.seriesDesc &&\n993: \t\tl.accept(\"0\") && l.accept(\"xX\") {\n994: \t\tl.accept(\"_\") // eg., 0X_1FFFP-16 == 0.1249847412109375\n995: \t\tdigitPattern = \"0123456789abcdefABCDEF\"\n996: \t}\n997: \tconst (\n998: \t\t// Define dot, exponent, and underscore patterns.\n999: \t\tdotPattern        = \".\"\n1000: \t\texponentPattern   = \"eE\"\n1001: \t\tunderscorePattern = \"_\"\n1002: \t\t// Anti-patterns are rune sets that cannot follow their respective rune.\n1003: \t\tdotAntiPattern        = \"_.\"\n1004: \t\texponentAntiPattern   = \"._eE\" // and EOL.\n1005: \t\tunderscoreAntiPattern = \"._eE\" // and EOL.\n1006: \t)\n1007: \t// All numbers follow the prefix: [.][d][d._eE]*\n1008: \tl.accept(dotPattern)\n1009: \tl.accept(digitPattern)\n1010: \t// [d._eE]* hereon.\n1011: \tdotConsumed := false\n1012: \texponentConsumed := false\n1013: \tfor l.is(digitPattern + dotPattern + underscorePattern + exponentPattern) {\n1014: \t\t// \".\" cannot repeat.\n1015: \t\tif l.is(dotPattern) {\n1016: \t\t\tif dotConsumed {\n1017: \t\t\t\tl.accept(dotPattern)\n1018: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1019: \t\t\t}\n1020: \t\t}\n1021: \t\t// \"eE\" cannot repeat.\n1022: \t\tif l.is(exponentPattern) {\n1023: \t\t\tif exponentConsumed {\n1024: \t\t\t\tl.accept(exponentPattern)\n1025: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1026: \t\t\t}\n1027: \t\t}\n1028: \t\t// Handle dots.\n1029: \t\tif l.accept(dotPattern) {\n1030: \t\t\tdotConsumed = true\n1031: \t\t\tif l.accept(dotAntiPattern) {\n1032: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1033: \t\t\t}\n1034: \t\t\t// Fractional hexadecimal literals are not allowed.\n1035: \t\t\tif len(digitPattern) > 10 /* 0x[\\da-fA-F].[\\d]+p[\\d] */ {\n1036: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1037: \t\t\t}\n1038: \t\t\tcontinue\n1039: \t\t}\n1040: \t\t// Handle exponents.\n1041: \t\tif l.accept(exponentPattern) {\n1042: \t\t\texponentConsumed = true\n1043: \t\t\tl.accept(\"+-\")\n1044: \t\t\tif l.accept(exponentAntiPattern) || l.peek() == eof {\n1045: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1046: \t\t\t}\n1047: \t\t\tcontinue\n1048: \t\t}\n1049: \t\t// Handle underscores.\n1050: \t\tif l.accept(underscorePattern) {\n1051: \t\t\tif l.accept(underscoreAntiPattern) || l.peek() == eof {\n1052: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1053: \t\t\t}\n1054: \n1055: \t\t\tcontinue\n1056: \t\t}\n1057: \t\t// Handle digits at the end since we already consumed before this loop.\n1058: \t\tl.acceptRun(digitPattern)\n1059: \t}\n1060: \t// Empty string is not a valid number.\n1061: \tif l.pos == initialPos {\n1062: \t\treturn false\n1063: \t}\n1064: \t// Next thing must not be alphanumeric unless it's the times token\n1065: \t// for series repetitions.\n1066: \tif r := l.peek(); (l.seriesDesc && r == 'x') || !isAlphaNumeric(r) {\n1067: \t\treturn true\n1068: \t}\n1069: \treturn false\n1070: }\n1071: \n1072: // lexIdentifier scans an alphanumeric identifier. The next character\n1073: // is known to be a letter.\n1074: func lexIdentifier(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n1075: \tfor isAlphaNumeric(l.next()) {\n1076: \t\t// absorb\n1077: \t}\n1078: \tl.backup()\n1079: \tl.emit(IDENTIFIER)\n1080: \treturn lexStatements\n1081: }\n1082: \n1083: // lexKeywordOrIdentifier scans an alphanumeric identifier which may contain\n1084: // a colon rune. If the identifier is a keyword the respective keyword Item\n1085: // is scanned.\n1086: func lexKeywordOrIdentifier(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n1087: Loop:\n1088: \tfor {\n1089: \t\tswitch r := l.next(); {\n1090: \t\tcase isAlphaNumeric(r) || r == ':':\n1091: \t\t\t// absorb.\n1092: \t\tdefault:\n1093: \t\t\tl.backup()\n1094: \t\t\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\n1095: \t\t\tswitch kw, ok := key[strings.ToLower(word)]; {\n1096: \t\t\tcase ok:\n1097: \t\t\t\t// For fill/fill_left/fill_right, only treat as keyword if followed by '('\n1098: \t\t\t\t// This allows using these as metric names (e.g., \"fill + fill\").\n1099: \t\t\t\t// This could be done for other keywords as well, but for the new fill\n1100: \t\t\t\t// modifiers this is especially important so we don't break any existing\n1101: \t\t\t\t// queries.\n1102: \t\t\t\tif kw == FILL || kw == FILL_LEFT || kw == FILL_RIGHT {\n1103: \t\t\t\t\tif !l.peekFollowedByLeftParen() {\n1104: \t\t\t\t\t\tl.emit(IDENTIFIER)\n1105: \t\t\t\t\t\tbreak Loop\n1106: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1107: \t\t\t\t}\n1108: \t\t\t\tl.emit(kw)\n1109: \t\t\tcase !strings.Contains(word, \":\"):\n1110: descriptions, duration expressions, and range vector syntax\\n\\n**Abstract Syntax Tree Definitions** (promql/parser/ast.go):\\n- `Expr` interface represents all expression types with `Type()` method for value type information\\n- Expression node types include: `VectorSelector` (metric selection with label matchers), `BinaryExpr` (arithmetic/logical operations), `AggregateExpr` (aggregation operations), `Call` (function calls), `MatrixSelector` (range vectors), `SubqueryExpr` (subqueries), `NumberLiteral`, `StringLiteral`, `ParenExpr`, `UnaryExpr`\\n- `Node` interface is the base for all AST nodes, supporting tree traversal via `Walk()`, `Inspect()`, and `ChildrenIter()` functions\\n- `VectorMatching` struct describes how vectors are matched in binary operations (one-to-one, Defines grammar rules for expressions, aggregations, binary operations, function calls, metric selectors, and histogram literals\\n- Integrates with the Lexer via the yyLexer interface for token consumption\\n- Uses semantic actions to build AST nodes during parsing\\n\\n**Function Registry** (promql/parser/functions.go):\\n- `Function` struct defines function metadata: name, argument types, descriptions, duration expressions, and range vector syntax\\n\\n**Abstract Syntax Tree Definitions** (promql/parser/ast.go):\\n- `Expr` interface represents all expression types with `Type()` method for value type information\\n- Expression node types include: `VectorSelector` (metric selection with label matchers), `BinaryExpr` (arithmetic/logical operations), `AggregateExpr` (aggregation operations), `Call` (function calls), `MatrixSelector` (range vectors), `SubqueryExpr` (subqueries), `NumberLiteral`, `StringLiteral`, `ParenExpr`, `UnaryExpr`\\n- `Node` interface is the base for all AST nodes, supporting tree traversal via `Walk()`, `Inspect()`, and `ChildrenIter()` functions\\n- `VectorMatching` struct describes how vectors are matched in binary operations (one-to-one, many-to-one, one-to-many, many-to-many cardinalities)\\n- Position tracking via `PositionRange` for error reporting\\n\\n**Yacc-Generated Parser** (promql/parser/generated_parser.y and Defines grammar rules for expressions, aggregations, binary operations, function calls, metric selectors, and histogram literals\\n- Integrates with the Lexer via the yyLexer interface for token consumption\\n- Uses semantic actions to build AST nodes during parsing\\n\\n**Function Registry** (promql/parser/functions.go):\\n- `Function` struct defines function metadata: name, argument types, Input query string → Lexer tokenization\\n2. Token stream → Yacc parser builds AST\\n3. AST → Type checking and semantic validation via checkAST()\\n4.
